Code 01: preparar datos
================
dacarras
Noviembre 23, 2022

# Preparación de datos

## Cargar datos desde archivo

``` r
#--------------------------------------------------------------------
# load data
#--------------------------------------------------------------------

#------------------------------------------------
# load data from file
#------------------------------------------------

data_iccs <- ilsa::iccs_2016
dplyr::glimpse(data_iccs)
```

## Cargar datos desde libreria

``` r
#--------------------------------------------------------------------
# folder locations
#--------------------------------------------------------------------

#------------------------------------------------
# install library
#------------------------------------------------

# devtools::install_github('dacarras/ilsa',force = TRUE)

#------------------------------------------------
# load data from library
#------------------------------------------------

data_iccs <- ilsa::iccs_2016
dplyr::glimpse(ilsa::remove_labels(data_iccs))
```

    ## 
    ## Attaching package: 'dplyr'

    ## 
    ##     filter, lag

    ## The following objects are masked from 'package:base':

``` r
data_svy    <- data_iccs %>%
              # remove labels
              ilsa::remove_labels() %>%
              # clustering
              mutate(id_i = seq(1:nrow(.))) %>%
              mutate(id_j = as.numeric(as.factor(paste0(COUNTRY, JKZONES, IDSCHOOL)))) %>%
              mutate(id_s = as.numeric(as.factor(paste0(COUNTRY, JKZONES)))) %>%
              mutate(id_r = as.numeric(as.factor(paste0(COUNTRY, JKZONES, JKREPS)))) %>%
              mutate(id_k = as.numeric(as.factor(paste0(COUNTRY)))) %>%
              # survey weights
              mutate(wt = TOTWGTS) %>%
              # students weights
              mutate(wi = WGTFAC2S*WGTADJ2S*WGTADJ3S) %>%
              # school weights
              mutate(wj = WGTFAC1*WGTADJ1S) %>%
              # create senate weights
              ilsa::senate_weights(., wt = 'wt', id_k = 'id_k', scale = 1000) %>%
              # create scaled weights
              ilsa::lsa_weights(., 
                id_i = 'id_i', 
                id_j = 'id_j', 
                id_k = 'id_k', 
                wt = 'wt', 
                wi = 'wi', 
                wj = 'wj') %>%
              dplyr::glimpse()
```

``` r
country_table <- read.table(
text="
COUNTRY  IDCNTRY   ctry_name

BGR      100       'Bulgaria'

EST      233       'Estonia'

HKG      344       'Hong Kong, SAR China'
HRV      191       'Croatia'

LTU      440       'Lithuania'
LVA      428       'Latvia'
MEX      484       'Mexico'

NLD      528       'Netherlands'

SVN      705       'Slovenia'

",
header=TRUE, stringsAsFactors = FALSE)
```

``` r
#------------------------------------------------
# add country names
#------------------------------------------------

library(dplyr)
data_cty   <- data_svy %>%
              dplyr::left_join(., 
                dplyr::select(country_table, COUNTRY, ctry_name), 
                by = 'COUNTRY') %>%
              dplyr::glimpse()
```

## Recodificar variables de interés

> Nota: no es necesario dicotimizar las variables originales. Los
> modelos de clases latentes pueden ser ajustados sobre matrices de
> respuesta con más de dos categorias. Para le primer ejemplo, acera de
> “civic norms”, categorizamos las variables originales, para tener
> resultados comparables a la literatura previa (Hooghe and Oser 2015;
> Hooghe et al. 2016). Para el segundo ejemplos, acerca de “concepto de
> democracia”, re-categorizamos las respuestas originales, para hacerlas
> interpretables en el modo de Quaranta (2019).

``` r
#--------------------------------------------------------------------
# responses to items
#--------------------------------------------------------------------

# -----------------------------------------------
# recode functions
# -----------------------------------------------

rec_1 <- function(x){
dplyr::case_when(
#  variable == old ~ new
  x == 1 ~ 1,
  x == 2 ~ 1,
  x == 3 ~ 0,
  x == 4 ~ 0,   
  TRUE ~ as.numeric(x))
# Note: it recodes likert type items,
#       where 1 is very important (1) and quite important (2)
#       and zero is not very important (3) and not important at all (4)
}

rec_2 <- function(x){
dplyr::case_when(
  x == 1 ~ 1, # good for democracy
  x == 2 ~ 0, # neither good or bad for democracy
  x == 3 ~ 0, # bad for democracy
  TRUE ~ as.numeric(x))
}

rec_3 <- function(x){
dplyr::case_when(
  x == 1 ~ 0, # good for democracy
  x == 2 ~ 0, # neither good or bad for democracy
  x == 3 ~ 1, # bad for democracy
  TRUE ~ as.numeric(x))
}

#------------------------------------------------
# recode original responses
#------------------------------------------------

library(dplyr)
data_items <- data_cty %>%
              # citizenship norms
              mutate(n01 = rec_1(IS3G23A)) %>% 
              mutate(n02 = rec_1(IS3G23B)) %>% 
              mutate(n03 = rec_1(IS3G23C)) %>% 
              mutate(n04 = rec_1(IS3G23D)) %>% 
              mutate(n05 = rec_1(IS3G23E)) %>% 
              mutate(n06 = rec_1(IS3G23F)) %>% 
              mutate(n07 = rec_1(IS3G23G)) %>% 
              mutate(n08 = rec_1(IS3G23H)) %>% 
              mutate(n09 = rec_1(IS3G23I)) %>% 
              mutate(n10 = rec_1(IS3G23J)) %>% 
              mutate(n11 = rec_1(IS3G23K)) %>% 
              mutate(n12 = rec_1(IS3G23L)) %>% 
              # concept of democracy
              mutate(td1 = rec_3(IS3G22A)) %>%
              mutate(td2 = rec_3(IS3G22B)) %>%
              mutate(td3 = rec_2(IS3G22C)) %>%
              mutate(td4 = rec_2(IS3G22D)) %>%
              mutate(td5 = rec_2(IS3G22E)) %>%
              mutate(td6 = rec_3(IS3G22F)) %>%
              mutate(td7 = rec_2(IS3G22G)) %>%
              mutate(td8 = rec_3(IS3G22H)) %>%
              mutate(td9 = rec_2(IS3G22I)) %>%
              dplyr::glimpse()
```

**Referencias**

Sandoval-Hernández, A., & Carrasco, D. (2020). A Measurement Strategy
for SDG Thematic Indicators 4.7.4 and 4.7.5 Using International Large
Scale Assessments in Education.
<http://tcg.uis.unesco.org/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2020/06/Measurement-Strategy-for-474-and-475-using-ILSA_20200625.pdf>

Hooghe, M., & Oser, J. (2015). The rise of engaged citizenship: The
evolution of citizenship norms among adolescents in 21 countries between
1999 and 2009. International Journal of Comparative Sociology, 56(1),
29–52. <https://doi.org/10.1177/0020715215578488>.

Hooghe, M., Oser, J., & Marien, S. (2016). A comparative analysis of
‘good citizenship’: A latent class analysis of adolescents’ citizenship
norms in 38 countries. International Political Science

Quaranta, M. (2019). What makes up democracy? Meanings of democracy and
their correlates among adolescents in 38 countries. Acta Politica,
0123456789. <https://doi.org/10.1057/s41269-019-00129-4>

## Selección de casos

> Nota: Seleccionamos muestras, solo para que la generación de
> resultados sea más rápida durante el taller.

``` r
#--------------------------------------------------------------------
# responses to items
#--------------------------------------------------------------------

#------------------------------------------------
# define random seed
#------------------------------------------------

set.seed(123)

#------------------------------------------------
# select 500 random cases per country
#------------------------------------------------

sel500  <- data_items %>%
           group_by(id_k) %>%
           sample_n(700, weights = ws, replace = FALSE) %>%
           ungroup() %>%           
           mutate(sel500 = 1) %>%
           dplyr::select(id_i, id_k, sel500)

#------------------------------------------------
# display table of selecion
#------------------------------------------------

dplyr::count(sel500, id_k, sel500)
```

    ## # A tibble: 24 × 3
    ##     id_k sel500     n

    ##  2     2      1   700
    ##  3     3      1   700
    ##  4     4      1   700
    ##  5     5      1   700
    ##  6     6      1   700
    ##  7     7      1   700
    ##  8     8      1   700
    ##  9     9      1   700
    ## 10    10      1   700
    ## # ℹ 14 more rows

``` r
#------------------------------------------------
# add selection dummy
#------------------------------------------------

data_flag  <- data_items %>%
              dplyr::left_join(., 
                dplyr::select(sel500, id_i, sel500), by = 'id_i') %>%
              mutate(sel500 = tidyr::replace_na(sel500, 0)) %>%
              dplyr::glimpse() 
```

``` r
library(dplyr)
data_civ  <- data_flag %>%
              dplyr::filter(ctry_name %in% 
                c(
                  'Chile',
                  'Colombia'

              dplyr::filter(sel500 == 1) %>%
              dplyr::select(id_i, ws, ctry_name, n01:td9) %>%
              dplyr::glimpse()
```

``` r
#------------------------------------------------
# subselection
#------------------------------------------------

sub_sel <- data_civ %>%
           group_by(ctry_name) %>%
           sample_n(350, weights = ws, replace = FALSE) %>%
           ungroup() %>%
           mutate(sub = 1) %>%
           dplyr::select(id_i, sub)

#------------------------------------------------
# sub sample data
#------------------------------------------------

library(dplyr)
data_exp   <- data_civ %>%
              dplyr::left_join(., sub_sel, by = 'id_i') %>%
              mutate(sub = tidyr::replace_na(sub, 0)) %>%
              dplyr::filter(sub == 1) %>%
              dplyr::glimpse()
```
